	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2016 Summer Olympics</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>

<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style="float:right"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Template:2016 Summer Olympics"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Template talk:2016 Summer Olympics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></div></div></td>
</tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>2016 Summer Olympics</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Jogos Olímpicos de Verão de 2016</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> officially known as the <b>Games of the XXXI Olympiad</b> and commonly known as <b>Rio 2016</b>, was an international <a href="/wiki/Multi-sport_event" title="Multi-sport event">multi-sport event</a> that was held from 5 to 21 August 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, with preliminary events in some sports beginning on 3 August. These were the first <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> ever to be held in <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a> and the fourth to be held in a <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/1968_Summer_Olympics" title="1968 Summer Olympics">1968 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, the <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympics" title="1980 Summer Olympics">1980 Summer Olympics</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.
</p><p>More than 11,000 athletes from 205 <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a>, including first time entrants <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Kosovo at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="South Sudan at the 2016 Summer Olympics">South Sudan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Refugee_Olympic_Team_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Refugee Olympic Team at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Refugee Olympic Team</a>, took part.<sup id="cite_ref-Olympic_Athletes_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Olympic_Athletes-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Rio2016_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rio2016-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> With 306 sets of medals, the games featured 28 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_sports" title="Olympic sports">Olympic sports</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Rugby_sevens" title="Rugby sevens">rugby sevens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, which were added to the Olympic program in 2009. These sporting events took place at 33 venues in the host city and at five separate venues in the Brazilian cities of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a>.
</p><p>These were the first Summer Olympic Games to take place under the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> (IOC) presidency of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bach" title="Thomas Bach">Thomas Bach</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rio2016_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rio2016-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The host city <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> was announced at the <a href="/wiki/121st_IOC_Session" title="121st IOC Session">121st</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_IOC_meetings" title="List of IOC meetings">IOC Session</a> in <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>, on 2 October 2009. Rio became the first South American city ever to host the Olympic Games. These were the first games to be held in a <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Portuguese-speaking country</a>, the first summer edition to be held entirely in the <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Brazil" title="Climate of Brazil">host country's winter season</a>, the first since <a href="/wiki/1968_Summer_Olympics" title="1968 Summer Olympics">1968</a> to be held in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>, and the first since <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000</a> to be held in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="United States at the 2016 Summer Olympics">United States</a> topped the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_medal_table" title="2016 Summer Olympics medal table">medal table</a>, winning the most gold and overall medals, 46 and 121, as well as its 1,000th Summer Olympic gold medal overall. <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Great Britain</a> finished second and became the second country of modern Olympics history to increase its tally of medals in the subsequent games after being the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Great Britain at the 2012 Summer Olympics">host nation</a>. <a href="/wiki/China_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="China at the 2016 Summer Olympics">China</a> finished third. Host country <a href="/wiki/Brazil_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Brazil at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Brazil</a> won seven gold medals, its most at any single Summer Olympics, finishing in thirteenth place. Bahrain, Fiji, Jordan, Kosovo, Puerto Rico, Singapore, Tajikistan, Ivory Coast, and Vietnam each won their first gold medals, as did the group of Independent Olympic Athletes (from Kuwait).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bidding_process">Bidding process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Bidding process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_Candidata_(Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG/220px-Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG/330px-Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG/440px-Cidade_Candidata_%28Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cidade_Candidata_(Rio_de_Janeiro_for_the_2016_Olympic_Games).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A young girl adds her signature in support of Rio de Janeiro's candidacy.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Several people dressed in formal attire sit behind a bench. There are repeated graphics behind them." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg/220px-Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg/330px-Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg/440px-Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="529" data-file-height="329" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_de_Janeiro_2016_press_conference.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The bid committee, led by <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Arthur_Nuzman" title="Carlos Arthur Nuzman">Carlos Arthur Nuzman</a>, giving a press conference.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bids_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Bids for the 2016 Summer Olympics">Bids for the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>The process for the 2016 Olympic Games was officially launched on 16 May 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The first step for each city was to submit an initial application to the International Olympic Committee by 13 September 2007, confirming their intention to bid. Completed official bid files, containing answers to a 25-question IOC form, were to be submitted by each 14 January 2008. Four candidate cities were chosen for the shortlist on 4 June 2008: <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>, which hosted the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Summer Olympics</a> and will host again in <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020</a>. The IOC did not promote <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a> to the candidature phase, despite scoring higher than selected candidate city Rio de Janeiro, because of their intent of hosting the Olympics in October, outside of the IOC's sporting calendar. <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baku" title="Baku">Baku</a> also failed to make the cut.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nawal_El_Moutawakel" title="Nawal El Moutawakel">Nawal El Moutawakel</a> of Morocco headed the 10-member Evaluation Commission, having also chaired the evaluation commission for the <a href="/wiki/Bids_for_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Bids for the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics bids</a>. The commission made on-site inspections in the second quarter of 2009. They issued a comprehensive technical appraisal for IOC members on 2 September, one month before elections.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many restrictions are in place designed to prevent bidding cities from communicating with or influencing directly the 115 voting members. Cities may not invite any IOC member to visit nor may they send anything that could be construed as a gift. Nonetheless, bidding cities invest large sums in their PR and media programs in an attempt to indirectly influence the IOC members by garnering domestic support, support from sports media and general international media.
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">Ultimately, you are communicating with just 115 people and each one has influencers and pressure groups but you are still speaking to no more than about 1,500 people, perhaps 5,000 in the broadest sense. It is not just about getting ads out there but it is about a targeted and very carefully planned campaign.
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="3" class="cquotecite" style="border: none; padding-right: 4%; font-size: smaller; line-height:normal; text-align: right;"><cite>—&#8202;Jon Tibbs, a consultant on the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_bid_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Tokyo bid for the 2016 Summer Olympics">Tokyo bid</a><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The final voting was held on 2 October 2009, in Copenhagen with Madrid and Rio de Janeiro perceived as favourites to land the games. Chicago and Tokyo were eliminated after the first and second rounds of voting, respectively, while Rio de Janeiro took a significant lead over Madrid heading into the final round. The lead held and Rio de Janeiro was announced as host of 2016 Summer Olympics.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_and_preparation">Development and preparation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development and preparation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 26 June 2011, it was reported on <a href="/wiki/AroundTheRings.com" class="mw-redirect" title="AroundTheRings.com">AroundTheRings.com</a> that Roderlei Generali, the COO of the Rio de Janeiro Organizing Committee for the Olympic Games, resigned just one year after taking the job at ROOC. This comes just five months after CCO Flávio Pestana quit for personal reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Pestana withdrew later during the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="2012 Summer Paralympics">2012 Summer Paralympics</a>. Renato Ciuchin was then appointed as COO.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues_and_infrastructure">Venues and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Venues and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Venues_of_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_and_Paralympics" title="Venues of the 2016 Summer Olympics and Paralympics">Venues of the 2016 Summer Olympics and Paralympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg/220px-Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg/330px-Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg/440px-Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1116" data-file-height="875" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_de_Janeiro_bid_venues_for_the_2016_Summer_Olympics.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Venues of the 2016 Summer Olympics</div></div></div>
<p>Events took place at eighteen existing venues, nine new venues constructed specifically for the Games, and seven temporary venues.<sup id="cite_ref-CF_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each event was held in one of four geographically segregated Olympic clusters: <a href="/wiki/Barra_da_Tijuca" title="Barra da Tijuca">Barra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copacabana_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Copacabana (Rio de Janeiro)">Copacabana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deodoro,_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Deodoro, Rio de Janeiro">Deodoro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_(neighborhood)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maracanã (neighborhood)">Maracanã</a>. The same was done for the <a href="/wiki/2007_Pan_American_Games" title="2007 Pan American Games">2007 Pan American Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Several of the venues were located at the Barra Cluster Olympic Park.<sup id="cite_ref-CF_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Athletes could access their venues in shorter than ten minutes and about 75 percent could do so in less than 25 minutes. Of the 34 competition locations, eight of them underwent permanent works, seven were limited, and nine were perpetual legacy venues.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The largest venue at the games in terms of <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> was the 74,738-seat <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã Stadium</a>, which served as the ceremonies venue and site of the football finals.<sup id="cite_ref-CF_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The second largest stadium was the 60,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Jo%C3%A3o_Havelange" class="mw-redirect" title="Estádio Olímpico João Havelange">Estádio Olímpico João Havelange</a>, which hosted track and field events.<sup id="cite_ref-CF_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CF-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The athletes' village was said to be the largest in Olympic history. Fittings included about 80,000 chairs, 70,000 tables, 29,000 mattresses, 60,000 clothes hangers, 6,000 television sets and 10,000 smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-rio2016.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rio2016.com-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_park">Olympic park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Olympic park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Barra_Olympic_Park" title="Barra Olympic Park">Barra Olympic Park</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/220px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/330px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/440px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Barra_Olympic_Park" title="Barra Olympic Park">Barra Olympic Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Barra Olympic Park is a cluster of nine sporting venues in <a href="/wiki/Barra_da_Tijuca" title="Barra da Tijuca">Barra da Tijuca</a>, in the west zone of Rio de Janeiro, Brazil. The site of the Olympic Park was formerly occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Internacional_Nelson_Piquet" title="Autódromo Internacional Nelson Piquet">Autódromo Internacional Nelson Piquet</a>, also known as Jacarepaguá.<sup id="cite_ref-abcnews-2013_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abcnews-2013-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The nine venues within the Olympic Park were:<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-federal-venues_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-federal-venues-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Carioca_Arena_1" title="Carioca Arena 1">Carioca Arena 1</a>: basketball (capacity: 16,000); <a href="/wiki/Carioca_Arena_2" title="Carioca Arena 2">Carioca Arena 2</a>: wrestling, judo (capacity: 10,000); <a href="/wiki/Carioca_Arena_3" title="Carioca Arena 3">Carioca Arena 3</a>: fencing, taekwondo (capacity: 10,000); <a href="/wiki/Future_Arena" title="Future Arena">Future Arena</a>: handball (capacity: 12,000); <a href="/wiki/Maria_Lenk_Aquatic_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Lenk Aquatic Center">Maria Lenk Aquatics Centre</a>: diving, synchronised swimming, water polo (capacity: 5,000); <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Aquatics_Stadium" title="Olympic Aquatics Stadium">Olympic Aquatics Stadium</a>: swimming, water polo play-offs (capacity: 15,000); <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Tennis_Centre_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" title="Olympic Tennis Centre (Rio de Janeiro)">Olympic Tennis Centre</a>: tennis (capacity: 10,000 Main Court); <a href="/wiki/HSBC_Arena_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="HSBC Arena (Rio de Janeiro)">Rio Olympic Arena</a>: gymnastics (capacity: 12,000); and <a href="/wiki/Rio_Olympic_Velodrome" title="Rio Olympic Velodrome">Rio Olympic Velodrome</a>: track cycling (capacity: 5,000).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Football at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>As well as the Estádio Olímpico João Havelange and Maracanã and in Rio de Janeiro, football matches took place at 5 venues in the cities of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manaus" title="Manaus">Manaus</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_renovation">Urban renovation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Urban renovation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Port of Rio de Janeiro">Port of Rio de Janeiro</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg/220px-VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg/330px-VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg/440px-VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:VLT_Rio_09_2016_3355.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mauá Square, with the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Tomorrow" title="Museum of Tomorrow">Museum of Tomorrow</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_Light_Rail" title="Rio de Janeiro Light Rail">light rail</a></div></div></div>
<p>Rio's historical <a href="/wiki/Centro_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Centro (Rio de Janeiro)">downtown</a> underwent an urban waterfront revitalization project called <i><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Port of Rio de Janeiro">Porto Maravilha</a></i>. It covers 5&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1.9&#160;sq&#160;mi) in area. The project aimed to redevelop the port area, increasing the city center's attractiveness and enhancing Rio's competitive position in the global economy.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The urban renovation involves: 700&#160;km (430&#160;mi) of public networks for water supply, sanitation, drainage, electricity, gas and telecom; 4&#160;km (2.5&#160;mi) of tunnels; 70&#160;km (43&#160;mi) of roads; 650&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (250&#160;sq&#160;mi) of sidewalks; 17&#160;km (11&#160;mi) of bike path; 15,000&#160;trees; three sanitation treatment plants. As part of this renovation, a new tram was built from the Santos Dumont Airport to Rodoviária Novo Rio. It was due to open in April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Games required more than 200 kilometres of security fencing. A 15,000 square metre warehouse in Barra da Tijuca in western Rio was used to assemble and supply the furniture and fittings for the Olympic Village. A second warehouse of 90,000 square metres, located in Duque de Caxias near the roads that provide access to the venues, contained all the equipment needed for the sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-rio2016.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rio2016.com-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medals">Medals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Medals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Medalhas_Rio_2016_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/220px-Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/330px-Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg/440px-Medalhas_Rio_2016_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3640" data-file-height="2425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Medalhas_Rio_2016_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 2016 Summer Olympics medals</div></div></div>
<p>The medal design was unveiled on 15 June 2016; they were produced by the <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_Moeda_do_Brasil" title="Casa da Moeda do Brasil">Casa da Moeda do Brasil</a>. The bronze and silver medals contained 30% recycled materials, while the gold medals were produced using gold that had been mined and extracted using means that met a series of sustainability criteria, such as being extracted without the use of mercury. The medals feature a wreath design, while the obverse, as is traditional, features <a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Nike</a>, the Greek goddess of victory. They were accompanied by a wooden carrying box, while medallists also received a trophy of the Games' emblem.<sup id="cite_ref-ioc-medaldesign_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-medaldesign-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo-noflowers_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-noflowers-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2017, an <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> article disclosed that more than 100 athletes from around the world reported that their medals had damage, including black spots, flaking, or surface degrading. Rio officials offered to replace any defective medals and found problems with 6 to 7 percent of all awarded medals.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Torch_relay">Torch relay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Torch relay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_torch_relay" title="2016 Summer Olympics torch relay">2016 Summer Olympics torch relay</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_(28605511640).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg/220px-Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg/330px-Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg/440px-Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_%2828605511640%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Passagem_da_Tocha_Ol%C3%ADmpica_em_SP_(28605511640).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Torch relay in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, with the basketball player <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Varej%C3%A3o" title="Anderson Varejão">Anderson Varejão</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_(29066118645).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg/220px-Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg/330px-Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg/440px-Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_%2829066118645%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5568" data-file-height="3712" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_-_Volunt%C3%A1rios_organizando_barreiras_(29066118645).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Volunteers working at the Olympic Stadium during the games.</div></div></div>
<p>The Olympic flame was lit at the temple of Hera in <a href="/wiki/Olympia,_Greece" title="Olympia, Greece">Olympia</a> on 21 April 2016, the traditional start of the Greek phase of the torch relay. On 27 April the flame was handed over to the Brazilian organisers at a ceremony at the <a href="/wiki/Panathenaic_Stadium" title="Panathenaic Stadium">Panathenaic Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>. A brief stop was made in Switzerland to visit the IOC headquarters and the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Museum" title="Olympic Museum">Olympic Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lausanne" title="Lausanne">Lausanne</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Geneva" title="United Nations Office at Geneva">United Nations Office at Geneva</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-starts_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-starts-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The torch relay began its Brazilian journey on 3 May at the capital <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>. The torch relay visited more than 300 Brazilian cities (including all the 26 states capitals and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_District_(Brazil)" title="Federal District (Brazil)">Brazilian Federal District</a>), with the last part held in the city of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio de Janeiro (city)">Rio de Janeiro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dressage_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dressage-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> lighting the cauldron during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2016 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">2016 Summer Olympics opening ceremony</a> on 5 August.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Volunteers">Volunteers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Volunteers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Unpaid volunteers performed a variety of tasks before and during the Games. A target of 50,000 volunteers was set as early as 2012. When recruitment took place in 2014, over 240,000 applications were received. The volunteers wore clothing which included yellow polo shirts and jackets, beige trousers, white socks and green trainers which they collected from the Uniform Distribution and Accreditation Centre. But many volunteers have stopped to due long working hours and one free meal a day.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Volunteers also wore photo accreditation badges which were also worn by officials, athletes, family members and media which gain them access to specific venues and buildings around the site.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ticketing">Ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ticket prices were announced on 16 September 2014, all of which were sold in <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_real" title="Brazilian real">Brazilian reais</a> (BRL). A total of 7.5 million tickets were to be sold in total, with ticket prices ranging from BRL 40 for many events to BRL 4,600 for the most expensive seats at the opening ceremony. About 3.8 million of these tickets were available for BRL 70 or less.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As an aspect of its bid, Rio's organizing committee planned to focus on <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_protection" title="Environmental protection">environmental protection</a> as a theme of these Games, going on to dub them a "Green Games for a Blue Planet".<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic-greengames_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-greengames-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> As legacy projects, organisers intended to introduce a wider array of public transport options, upgrade the infrastructure of the <a href="/wiki/Favelas" class="mw-redirect" title="Favelas">favelas</a> to provide improved transport and access to utilities, upgrade Rio's sewer system in order to remediate the level of pollution in the <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay" title="Guanabara Bay">Guanabara Bay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic-greengames_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-greengames-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian-fundingclean_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-fundingclean-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and plant 24 million seedlings to offset the expected carbon emissions of the Games. However, some of these projects were met with delays or faced with economic shortfalls, which led some critics to believe that Rio would not be able to accomplish them.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic-greengames_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic-greengames-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vicenews-enviro_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vicenews-enviro-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg/220px-Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg/330px-Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg/440px-Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arena_do_Futuro_Rio_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Future_Arena" title="Future Arena">Future Arena</a>, a temporary venue designed to be reconstructed into schools.</div></div></div>
<p>The focus on environmental protection also influenced the implementation of certain Olympic protocols: the Olympic cauldron was designed to be smaller than previous iterations in order to reduce emissions, and used a <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_sculpture" class="mw-redirect" title="Kinetic sculpture">kinetic sculpture</a> to enhance its appearance in lieu of a larger body of flames.<sup id="cite_ref-dezeen-cauldron_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dezeen-cauldron-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The bronze and silver medals, as well as ribbons on all medals, incorporate recycled materials.<sup id="cite_ref-ioc-medaldesign_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ioc-medaldesign-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yahoo-noflowers_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-noflowers-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The athletes were not presented with flowers during medal ceremonies, as had been traditionally done at prior Olympics (although flowers were still used as part of the staging of medal presentations). Organisers considered the practice to be wasteful since they were often thrown away, and "would struggle to survive in the tropical Brazilian climate" if kept. The podiums were also designed so that their materials could be recycled to make furniture.<sup id="cite_ref-yahoo-noflowers_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahoo-noflowers-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mashable-noflowers_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mashable-noflowers-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Future_Arena" title="Future Arena">Future Arena</a>, host of handball competitions, was designed as a modular temporary venue whose components can be reconstructed to build schools.<sup id="cite_ref-dezeen-futurearena_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dezeen-futurearena-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> However, as of November 2017, the arena is still standing because of lack of money to dismantle it and no allocation of funds to do so in the 2018 budget.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Portions of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2016 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">opening ceremony</a> were also dedicated to the issue of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-huff-climatechange_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huff-climatechange-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Games">The Games</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Games">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_ceremony">Opening ceremony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Opening ceremony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony" title="2016 Summer Olympics opening ceremony">2016 Summer Olympics opening ceremony</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_Parade_of_Nations" title="2016 Summer Olympics Parade of Nations">2016 Summer Olympics Parade of Nations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg/220px-2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg/330px-2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg/440px-2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2016_Summer_Olympics_opening_ceremony_1035301-05082016-_v9a2048_04.08.16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A scene from the opening ceremony.</div></div></div>
<p>The opening ceremony took place at <a href="/wiki/Maracana_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Maracana Stadium">Maracana Stadium</a> on 5 August 2016, and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Meirelles" title="Fernando Meirelles">Fernando Meirelles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Thomas" title="Daniela Thomas">Daniela Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrucha_Waddington" title="Andrucha Waddington">Andrucha Waddington</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The ceremony highlighted aspects of Brazilian history and culture, and featured a segment narrated by <a href="/wiki/Fernanda_Montenegro" title="Fernanda Montenegro">Fernanda Montenegro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Judi_Dench" title="Judi Dench">Judi Dench</a> with an appeal to <a href="/wiki/Environmental_conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental conservation">environmental conservation</a> and preventing <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-huff-climatechange_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huff-climatechange-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-torstar-ochighlights_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torstar-ochighlights-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The ceremony also featured the inaugural presentation of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Laurel" title="Olympic Laurel">Olympic Laurel</a>, an honour bestowed by the IOC to those that have made "significant achievements in education, culture, development and peace through sport", to <a href="/wiki/Kipchoge_Keino" title="Kipchoge Keino">Kipchoge "Kip" Keino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The Games were officially opened by Acting <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President of Brazil</a> <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Olympic cauldron was lit by <a href="/wiki/Vanderlei_Cordeiro_de_Lima" class="mw-redirect" title="Vanderlei Cordeiro de Lima">Vanderlei Cordeiro de Lima</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2004_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_marathon" title="Athletics at the 2004 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s marathon">men's marathon</a> bronze medallist at the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004 Summer Olympics</a> who was also awarded the <a href="/wiki/Pierre_de_Coubertin_medal" title="Pierre de Coubertin medal">Pierre de Coubertin medal</a> for sportsmanship by the IOC after being attacked by a spectator and losing his lead. The cauldron was originally expected to be lit by Brazilian footballer <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pelé">Pelé</a>, but he declined to participate due to health problems.<sup id="cite_ref-torstar-ochighlights_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torstar-ochighlights-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the opening ceremony, a public cauldron was lit in front of the <a href="/wiki/Candel%C3%A1ria_Church" title="Candelária Church">Candelária Church</a> by Jorge Gomes, a 14-year-old Brazilian athlete who had escaped from poverty to train as a runner.<sup id="cite_ref-cbcnews-outdoorcauldron_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbcnews-outdoorcauldron-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jorge_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jorge-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/220px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/330px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/440px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_009_8214_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Youth_Arena" title="Youth Arena">Youth Arena</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg/220px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg/330px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg/440px-Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_ZonaB_Deodoro_014_2480_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Deodoro_Stadium" title="Deodoro Stadium">Deodoro Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg/220px-Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg/330px-Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg/440px-Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vis%C3%A3o_da_arquibancada_da_pista_olimpica_BMX1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympic_BMX_Centre" title="Olympic BMX Centre">Olympic BMX Centre</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg/220px-Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg/330px-Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg/440px-Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Golfe_Rio_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympic_golf_course_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic golf course (Rio de Janeiro)">Olympic Golf Course</a></div></div></div>
<p>The 2016 Summer Olympic programme featured 28 sports encompassing 306 events. The number of events in each discipline is noted in parentheses.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_sports">New sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: New sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/121st_IOC_Session" title="121st IOC Session">121st IOC Session</a></div>
<p>In April 2008, the IOC began accepting applications for two new sports to be introduced to the Olympic programme, which included baseball and <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> (which were dropped in 2005), <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Squash_(sport)" title="Squash (sport)">squash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roller_sports" class="mw-redirect" title="Roller sports">roller sports</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> all applied to be included. Formal presentations were held for the IOC executive board in June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August, the executive board initially gave its approval to <a href="/wiki/Rugby_sevens" title="Rugby sevens">rugby sevens</a>—a seven-player version of rugby union—by a majority vote, thus removing baseball, roller sports, and squash from contention; leaving golf, karate, and rugby sevens. A final vote was held on 9 October 2009, the final day of the 121st IOC Session. A new system was in place at this session; a sport now needed only a simple majority from the full IOC committee for approval rather than the two-thirds majority previously required.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Sailing_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="International Sailing Federation">International Sailing Federation</a> announced in May 2012 that <a href="/wiki/Windsurfing" title="Windsurfing">windsurfing</a> would be replaced at the 2016 Olympics by <a href="/wiki/Kitesurfing" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitesurfing">kitesurfing</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> but this decision was reversed in November.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 121st IOC Session decided to add Rugby Sevens and Golf to the Rio 2016 program.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The tally for rugby was 81 in favor, with 8 against,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and golf was approved 63–26.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Neither sport is new to the Olympics — rugby was last featured at the Olympics <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_at_the_1924_Summer_Olympics" title="Rugby union at the 1924 Summer Olympics">in 1924</a>, and golf <a href="/wiki/Golf_at_the_1904_Summer_Olympics" title="Golf at the 1904 Summer Olympics">in 1904</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Participating_National_Olympic_Committees">Participating National Olympic Committees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Participating National Olympic Committees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/220px-Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/330px-Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg/440px-Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio2016_julho_VilaAtletas_Barra_002_2659_-c-2016_GabrielHeusi_HeusiAction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rio_2016_Olympic_Village" title="Rio 2016 Olympic Village">Rio 2016 Olympic Village</a></div></div></div>
<p>All 206 <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committees</a> have qualified at least one athlete.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The first three nations to qualify athletes for the Games were Germany, Great Britain, and the Netherlands who each qualified four athletes for the team dressage by winning medals in the team event at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FEI_World_Equestrian_Games" title="2014 FEI World Equestrian Games">2014 FEI World Equestrian Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As host nation, Brazil has received automatic entry for some sports including in all cycling disciplines and six places for weightlifting events.<sup id="cite_ref-cyclingquotas_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cyclingquotas-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-brazilweightlifting_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brazilweightlifting-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2016 Summer Olympics were the first games in which <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Kosovo at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Kosovo</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="South Sudan at the 2016 Summer Olympics">South Sudan</a> were eligible to participate. <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgarian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> weightlifters were banned from Rio Olympics for numerous anti-doping violations.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a> was banned in October 2015 for the second time in five years over government interference in the country's Olympic committee.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugee_athletes">Refugee athletes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Refugee athletes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Refugee_Olympic_Team_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Refugee Olympic Team at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Refugee Olympic Team at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg/220px-Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg/330px-Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg/440px-Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3356" data-file-height="2234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_Refugees_1033413-29072016-_dsc1069.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Refugee Olympic team arriving in Rio de Janeiro</div></div></div>
<p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">European migrant crisis</a> and other reasons, the IOC allowed athletes to compete as <a href="/wiki/Independent_Olympians_at_the_Olympic_Games" title="Independent Olympians at the Olympic Games">Independent Olympians</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Flag">Olympic Flag</a>. In <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">the previous Summer Olympic Games</a>, refugees were ineligible to compete because of their inability to represent their home NOCs.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> On 2 March 2016, the IOC finalised plans for a specific <a href="/wiki/Refugee_Olympic_Athletes_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Refugee Olympic Athletes at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Refugee Olympic Team (ROT)</a>; out of 43 refugee athletes deemed potentially eligible, 10 were chosen to form the team.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC-ROA_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-ROA-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_athletes">Independent athletes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Independent athletes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Independent_Olympic_Athletes_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Independent Olympic Athletes at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Independent Olympic Athletes at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>Due to the suspension of the National Olympic Committee of Kuwait, participants from Kuwait were allowed to participate under the Olympic Flag as Independent Olympic Athletes.
</p><p>In November 2015, <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Russia at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Russia</a> was provisionally suspended from all international track and field athletic competitions by the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Athletics_Federations" title="International Association of Athletics Federations">International Association of Athletics Federations</a> (IAAF) following a <a href="/wiki/World_Anti-Doping_Agency" title="World Anti-Doping Agency">World Anti-Doping Agency</a> (WADA) report into a <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_Russia" title="Doping in Russia">doping program</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.com_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.com-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The IAAF announced that it would allow individual Russian athletes to apply for "exceptional eligibility" to participate in the Games as "neutral" athletes, if it were independently verified that they had not engaged in doping nor in the Russian doping program.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-yuliya2_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-yuliya2-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 July 2016, the IOC rejected the IAAF and WADA's recommendations to allow athletes to compete neutrally, stating that the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Charter" title="Olympic Charter">Olympic Charter</a> "does not foresee such 'neutral athletes'" and that it was up to each country's National Olympic Committee to decide which athletes would be competing.<sup id="cite_ref-:322_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:322-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Russian athletes competed under the Russian flag, although they would compete under a neutral flag in the <a href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympics" title="2018 Winter Olympics">2018 Winter Olympics</a> following several developments with regard to the doping investigation.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_houses">National houses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: National houses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the Games some countries and continents had a national house. These temporary meeting places for supporters, athletes and other followers were located throughout Rio de Janeiro.<sup id="cite_ref-nationalhouses_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nationalhouses-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calendar">Calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chronological_summary_of_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Chronological summary of the 2016 Summer Olympics">Chronological summary of the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Records">Records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Records">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_and_Olympic_records_set_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="World and Olympic records set at the 2016 Summer Olympics">World and Olympic records set at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>Twenty-seven world records and ninety-one Olympic records were set during the 2016 Summer Olympics. The records were set in archery, athletics, canoeing, cycling track, modern pentathlon, rowing, shooting, swimming and weightlifting.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medal_table">Medal table</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Medal table">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg/220px-Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg/330px-Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg/440px-Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4025" data-file-height="2678" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Medalhas_Rio_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The medals designed for the Olympics. They were designed to be environmentally friendly from recycled materials.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_medal_table" title="2016 Summer Olympics medal table">2016 Summer Olympics medal table</a></div>
<p>The top ten listed <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committees" class="mw-redirect" title="National Olympic Committees">NOCs</a> by number of gold medals are listed below. Host nation Brazil finished in 13th place with a total of 19 medals (7 gold, 6 silver, and 6 bronze).
</p>
