<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Event_scheduling">Event scheduling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Event scheduling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg/220px-Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg/330px-Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg/440px-Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3924" data-file-height="2834" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Candel%C3%A1ria_cauldron_at_2016_Summer_Olympics.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The public cauldron, located outside the <a href="/wiki/Candel%C3%A1ria_Church" title="Candelária Church">Candelária Church</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>A number of events, most notably in aquatics, beach volleyball, and track and field, were scheduled with sessions and matches occurring as late as 10:00&#160;p.m. to midnight BRT. These scheduling practices were influenced primarily by United States broadcast rightsholder <a href="/wiki/Olympics_on_NBC" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympics on NBC">NBC</a> – NBC's substantial rights fees are  one of the major sources of revenue for the IOC, therefore it has allowed the network to have influence on event scheduling to maximize U.S. television ratings when possible (NBC agreed to a US$7.75 billion contract extension on May 7, 2014, to air the Olympics through 2032, including US$1.23 billion for Rio 2016)<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> as well as the main Brazilian rightsholder <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a>. As Brasília time is only one hour ahead of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">Eastern Time Zone</a>, certain marquee events were scheduled to occur during U.S. <a href="/wiki/Primetime" class="mw-redirect" title="Primetime">primetime</a> hours (traditionally 8:00 to 11:00&#160;p.m. ET, 9:00&#160;p.m. to midnight BRT) allowing them to be broadcast live on the east coast as opposed to being <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_delay" title="Broadcast delay">delayed</a>. This practice was also to the benefit of Globo: a Brazilian critic noted that the network very rarely pre-empts its primetime <a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">telenovelas</a>, as they are among the highest-rated programs in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc-midnightmadness_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-midnightmadness-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-couriermail-latenight_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-couriermail-latenight-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-globonovelas_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-globonovelas-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Closing_ceremony">Closing ceremony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Closing ceremony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony" title="2016 Summer Olympics closing ceremony">2016 Summer Olympics closing ceremony</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_closing_ceremony_flag_bearers" title="2016 Summer Olympics closing ceremony flag bearers">2016 Summer Olympics closing ceremony flag bearers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_(29040726262).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg/220px-Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg/330px-Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg/440px-Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_%2829040726262%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3800" data-file-height="2533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminam_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_Rio_2016_(29040726262).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2016 Summer Olympics closing ceremony at <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games_ceremony#Closing" title="Olympic Games ceremony">closing ceremony</a> of the 2016 Summer Olympics was held on 21 August 2016 from 20:00 to 22:50 BRT at the <a href="/wiki/Maracan%C3%A3_Stadium" title="Maracanã Stadium">Maracanã Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> As per traditional Olympic protocol, the ceremony featured cultural presentations from both the current (Brazil) and following (Japan) host countries, as well as closing remarks by IOC president <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bach" title="Thomas Bach">Thomas Bach</a> and the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Organizing_Committee_of_the_Olympic_and_Paralympic_Games_Rio_2016" title="Organizing Committee of the Olympic and Paralympic Games Rio 2016">Games' organizing committee</a> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Arthur_Nuzman" title="Carlos Arthur Nuzman">Carlos Arthur Nuzman</a>, the official handover of the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_symbols#Flag" title="Olympic symbols">Olympic flag</a> from Rio de Janeiro mayor <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Paes" title="Eduardo Paes">Eduardo Paes</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> governor <a href="/wiki/Yuriko_Koike" title="Yuriko Koike">Yuriko Koike</a>, whose city will host the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a>, and the extinguishing of the Olympic flame.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The creative director for the ceremony was <a href="/wiki/Rosa_Magalh%C3%A3es" title="Rosa Magalhães">Rosa Magalhães</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Amid heavy rainfall, the ceremony began with interpretive dancers representing various landmarks in the host city. <a href="/wiki/Martinho_da_Vila" title="Martinho da Vila">Martinho da Vila</a> then performed a rendition of the classic song "<i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Carinhoso_(song)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Carinhoso (song) (page does not exist)">Carinhoso</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carinhoso" class="extiw" title="pt:Carinhoso">pt</a>&#93;</span></i>" by <a href="/wiki/Pixinguinha" title="Pixinguinha">Pixinguinha</a>. In another segment, introducing the athletes, pop singer <a href="/wiki/Roberta_S%C3%A1" title="Roberta Sá">Roberta Sá</a> channeled <a href="/wiki/Carmen_Miranda" title="Carmen Miranda">Carmen Miranda</a>, the fruit-headdress-wearing, midcentury Hollywood diva who endures as a beloved <a href="/wiki/Camp_(style)" title="Camp (style)">camp figure</a>. The Parade of Flags followed shortly after a choir of 27 children, representing the <a href="/wiki/States_of_Brazil" title="States of Brazil">states of Brazil</a>, sang the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_National_Anthem" title="Brazilian National Anthem">Brazilian national anthem</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg/220px-Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg/330px-Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg/440px-Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1130" data-file-height="753" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_Deodoro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Deodoro_Olympic_Whitewater_Stadium" title="Deodoro Olympic Whitewater Stadium">Deodoro Olympic Whitewater Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <i>Oxford Olympics Study 2016</i> estimated the out-turn cost of the Rio 2016 Summer Olympics at US$4.6 billion in 2015-dollars. This figure included sports-related costs, that is, (i) <i>operational costs</i> incurred by the organizing committee for the purpose of staging the Games, of which the largest components were technology, transportation, workforce, and administration costs, while other operational costs included security, catering, ceremonies, and medical services, and (ii) <i>direct capital costs</i> incurred by the host city and country or private investors to build the competition venues, the Olympic village, international broadcast center, and media and press center, which were required to host the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-cost_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cost-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Indirect capital costs were <i>not</i> included, such as for road, rail, or airport infrastructure, or for hotel upgrades or other business investment incurred in preparation for the Games but not directly related to staging the Games. The Rio Olympics' cost of US$4.6 billion compares with costs of US$40–44 billion for <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">Beijing 2008</a> and US$51 billion for <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">Sochi 2014</a>, the two most expensive Olympics in history. The average cost of the Summer Games since 1960 is US$5.2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-cost_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cost-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:908px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg" class="image" title="Barra Olympic Park"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg/900px-Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="900" height="198" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg/1350px-Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg/1800px-Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="1080" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zona_Ol%C3%ADmpica_da_Barra_da_Tijuca_-_Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_RIO_2016.jpg" title="File:Zona Olímpica da Barra da Tijuca - Parque Olímpico RIO 2016.jpg"> </a></div><center><a href="/wiki/Barra_Olympic_Park" title="Barra Olympic Park">Barra Olympic Park</a></center></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_2016_Summer_Olympics_broadcasters" title="List of 2016 Summer Olympics broadcasters">List of 2016 Summer Olympics broadcasters</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg/220px-Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg/330px-Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg/440px-Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2387" data-file-height="1773" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_de_M%C3%ADdia_Rio_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>International Broadcast Centre, at <a href="/wiki/Barra_Olympic_Park" title="Barra Olympic Park">Barra Olympic Park</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Broadcasting_Services" title="Olympic Broadcasting Services">Olympic Broadcasting Services</a> served as the host broadcaster for these Games; produced from a total of 7 mobile units, OBS distributed 40,000 hours of television footage and 60,000 hours of digital footage of the Games to its international rightsholders; for the first time in Olympic history, digital-oriented footage exceeded the amount of television-oriented footage. The International Broadcast Centre was constructed in the Barra da Tijuca cluster.<sup id="cite_ref-tvt-broadcasting_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tvt-broadcasting-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NHK" title="NHK">NHK</a> and OBS once again filmed portions of the Games, including the opening ceremony and selected events, in <a href="/wiki/8K_resolution" title="8K resolution">8K resolution</a> video. Additionally, expanding upon a 180-degree trial at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Winter_Youth_Olympics" title="2016 Winter Youth Olympics">2016 Winter Youth Olympics</a>, 85 hours of video content were originated in <a href="/wiki/360-degree_video" title="360-degree video">360-degree</a> <a href="/wiki/Virtual_reality" title="Virtual reality">virtual reality</a> formats.<sup id="cite_ref-variety-olympicsvr_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety-olympicsvr-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, <a href="/wiki/Olympics_on_NBC" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympics on NBC">NBC</a> offered <a href="/wiki/4K_resolution" title="4K resolution">4K</a> content, downconverted from the 8K footage and with <a href="/wiki/HDR_video" class="mw-redirect" title="HDR video">HDR</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolby_Atmos" title="Dolby Atmos">Dolby Atmos</a> support, to participating television providers.<sup id="cite_ref-thr-4kolympics_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thr-4kolympics-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Owing to their expertise in domestic broadcasts of the new sports introduced in Rio, <a href="/wiki/Golf_Channel_on_NBC" title="Golf Channel on NBC">NBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Television_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sky Television (New Zealand)">Sky New Zealand</a> staff handled the production of the golf and rugby sevens events on behalf of OBS.<sup id="cite_ref-tvt-broadcasting_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tvt-broadcasting-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2009, the IOC reached a deal to sell domestic broadcast rights to the 2016 Summer Olympics to <a href="/wiki/Grupo_Globo" title="Grupo Globo">Grupo Globo</a>. Replacing <a href="/wiki/RecordTV" title="RecordTV">Record TV</a> the deal covers free-to-air coverage on <a href="/wiki/Rede_Globo" title="Rede Globo">Rede Globo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Globosat" title="Globosat">pay TV</a>, and digital rights to the Games. In turn, Globo sub-licensed partial free-to-air rights to Rede Record, along with <a href="/wiki/Rede_Bandeirantes" title="Rede Bandeirantes">Rede Bandeirantes</a>. IOC board member <a href="/wiki/Richard_Carri%C3%B3n" title="Richard Carrión">Richard Carrión</a> described the agreement as "unprecedented", touting that "by working with Brazil's leading media organizations, we are confident that this represents a great deal for Olympic fans in the region. There will be a huge increase in the amount of Olympic action broadcast, both during and outside Games time, and Brazilians will have more choice of how, when and where they follow their Olympic Games."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympic_Golden_Rings_Awards">Olympic Golden Rings Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Olympic Golden Rings Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_(28430991164).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg/220px-Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg/330px-Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg/440px-Rio_2016_%2828430991164%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rio_2016_(28430991164).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Olympic_rings" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic rings">Olympic rings</a> displayed in Rio de Janeiro.</div></div></div>
<p>Following the conclusion of the games the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> in November 2017 announced the winners of the Golden rings in six categories for the best broadcast coverage of the games. The Best Olympic Sports Production was awarded to Beach Volleyball. It was produced by Geoff Johnson. and directed by Greg Breakell and Gary Milkis. The production for the cycling road race and Sailing came second and third. The next category was best Olympic feature. <a href="/wiki/TV_Globo" class="mw-redirect" title="TV Globo">TV Globo's</a> feature entitle "Esporte  Espetacular" finished third and <a href="/wiki/China_Central_Television" title="China Central Television">China Central Television's</a> feature - A Sequel of Love came second. The winner was <a href="/wiki/NBC_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="NBC Olympics">NBC Olympics</a> for their feature titled The Most Beautiful Thing. The third category was The Best Athlete Profile. RTBF Radio Télévision de la Communauté Française de Belgique for their profile of <a href="/wiki/Nafi_Thiam" class="mw-redirect" title="Nafi Thiam">Nafi Thiam</a> collected the third place prize. TV Globo went one better than the previous category coming second with their profile of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Izaquias_Queiroz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Izaquias Queiroz (page does not exist)">Izaquias Queiroz</a>. The winner of the category again was NBC this time for their piece on <a href="/wiki/Wayde_van_Niekerk" title="Wayde van Niekerk">Wayde van Niekerk</a>. The Best On-Air Promotion was announced next with the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> winning with NBC this time coming second and <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Television" title="Bulgarian National Television">Bulgarian National Television</a> finished third. The Best Olympic Digital Service went to NBC with ZDF-German TV and SporTV/Globosat picking up the second and third places. The Best Olympic Programme was awarded to SporTV/Globosat while TV Globo and BBC Sport completed the podium.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics_marketing" title="2016 Summer Olympics marketing">2016 Summer Olympics marketing</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascots">Mascots</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Mascots">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Vinicius_and_Tom" title="Vinicius and Tom">Vinicius and Tom</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vinicius_and_Tom.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/62/Vinicius_and_Tom.svg/220px-Vinicius_and_Tom.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/62/Vinicius_and_Tom.svg/330px-Vinicius_and_Tom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/62/Vinicius_and_Tom.svg/440px-Vinicius_and_Tom.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="202" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vinicius_and_Tom.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vinicius_and_Tom" title="Vinicius and Tom">Vinicius</a> (left), the mascot of the Rio 2016, and <a href="/wiki/Vinicius_and_Tom" title="Vinicius and Tom">Tom</a> (right), the mascot of the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Paralympics" title="2016 Summer Paralympics">2016 Summer Paralympics</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Olympic_mascots" title="List of Olympic mascots">official mascots</a> of the 2016 Summer Olympics and Paralympics were unveiled on 24 November 2014. They were created by <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo">Sao Paulo</a>-based animation company Birdo.<sup id="cite_ref-MascotNames_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MascotNames-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The Olympic mascot <a href="/wiki/Vinicius_and_Tom" title="Vinicius and Tom">Vinicius</a>, named after musician <a href="/wiki/Vinicius_de_Moraes" title="Vinicius de Moraes">Vinicius de Moraes</a>, represents Brazilian wildlife and carries design traits of cats, monkeys, and birds.<sup id="cite_ref-MascotNames_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MascotNames-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> According to their fictional backgrounds, the mascots "were both born from the joy of Brazilians after it was announced that Rio would host the Games."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Brand director Beth Lula stated that the mascots were intended to reflect the diversity of Brazil's culture and people.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-riomascot_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-riomascot-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The names of the mascots were determined by a public vote whose results were announced on 14 December 2014; the names, which reference the co-writers of the song "<a href="/wiki/The_Girl_from_Ipanema" title="The Girl from Ipanema">The Girl from Ipanema</a>", won over two other sets of names, tallying 44 percent of 323,327 votes.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Wrestling_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Wrestling at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Olympic wrestling events</a>, coaches were given plush dolls of Vinicius to throw into the ring when they wished to challenge a referee's call.<sup id="cite_ref-Gordon_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emblem">Emblem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Emblem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_(28370259403).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg/220px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg/330px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg/440px-Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_%2828370259403%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Rio_2016_(28370259403).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sculpture of the logo of the Rio 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Barra_Olympic_Park" title="Barra Olympic Park">Barra Olympic Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>The official emblem for the 2016 Summer Olympics was designed by the Brazilian agency Tatíl Design and unveiled on 31 December 2010, winning in a competition against 139 agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-adweek_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adweek-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The logo represents three figures joined at their arms and feet, with the overall shape reflecting that of <a href="/wiki/Sugarloaf_Mountain_(Brazil)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sugarloaf Mountain (Brazil)">Sugarloaf Mountain</a>. The emblem was also designed to have a three-dimensional form, which designer Fred Gelli claimed made it the "first 3D logo in the history of the Olympics."<sup id="cite_ref-dezeen-16emblem_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dezeen-16emblem-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The logo has been noted as evoking <a href="/wiki/Henri_Matisse" title="Henri Matisse">Henri Matisse</a>'s painting <i><a href="/wiki/Dance_(Matisse)" title="Dance (Matisse)">Dance</a></i>. There were also allegations by the Colorado-based Telluride Foundation that the logo had been plagiarised from its own. While also consisting of several figures linked in motion, the Telluride Foundation logo contains four figures. This is not the first time that the foundation had alleged plagiarism of its logo by a Brazilian event; in 2004, the linked figures element had been copied for the logo of <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Carnival" title="Brazilian Carnival">Carnival</a> celebrations in <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a>. Gelli defended the allegations, stating that the concept of figures linked in embrace was not inherently original as it was "an ancient reference" and "in the <a href="/wiki/Collective_unconscious" title="Collective unconscious">collective unconscious</a>". Gelli cited <i>Dance</i> as an influence of the logo's concept, and stated that the designers had intentionally aimed to make the interpretation of the concept as dissimilar to others as possible.<sup id="cite_ref-denverpost-telluride_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-denverpost-telluride-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concerns_and_controversies">Concerns and controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Concerns and controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Concerns_and_controversies_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Concerns and controversies at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Concerns and controversies at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>The lead-up to these Games was marked by <a href="/wiki/Concerns_and_controversies_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Concerns and controversies at the 2016 Summer Olympics">controversies</a>, including the Brazil's <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_Brazilian_economic_crisis" title="2014 Brazilian economic crisis">economic crisis</a>; the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Zika_virus_epidemic" title="2015–16 Zika virus epidemic">Zika virus epidemic</a> and the significant <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay#Environment" title="Guanabara Bay">pollution in the Guanabara Bay</a>; and a <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_Russia" title="Doping in Russia">doping scandal</a> involving <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Russia at the 2016 Summer Olympics">Russia</a>, which affected the participation of its athletes in the Games. However, nobody competing in or attending the Olympics contracted the Zika virus<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> and the Games took place normally, without any major incident.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_economic_crisis">Political and economic crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Political and economic crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/2014_Brazilian_economic_crisis" title="2014 Brazilian economic crisis">2014 Brazilian economic crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">Operation Car Wash</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:01062016-_89A3476-Editar_(27244602030).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg/220px-01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg/330px-01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg/440px-01062016-_89A3476-Editar_%2827244602030%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3506" data-file-height="1978" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:01062016-_89A3476-Editar_(27244602030).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Suspended president <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> during an interview with <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Alvorada_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Alvorada Palace">Alvorada Palace</a>, 1 June 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>In 2014, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Car_Wash" title="Operation Car Wash">Operation Car Wash</a>, an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_of_Brazil" title="Federal Police of Brazil">Federal Police of Brazil</a>, uncovered unprecedented <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> and corruption at the state-controlled oil company <a href="/wiki/Petrobras" title="Petrobras">Petrobras</a>. In early 2015, a series of protests against alleged corruption by the government of President <a href="/wiki/Dilma_Rousseff" title="Dilma Rousseff">Dilma Rousseff</a> began in Brazil, triggered by revelations that numerous politicians were involved in the Petrobras affair. By early 2016, the scandal had escalated into a full-blown political crisis affecting not only President Rousseff, but also former President <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva</a>, resulting in <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_protests_in_Brazil" title="2015–16 protests in Brazil">massive demonstrations all over the country involving millions of protesters</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> both anti and pro-Rousseff.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> At the same time, Brazil faced its worst economic recession since the 1990s, raising questions about whether the country was adequately prepared for the Games against a volatile political and economic backdrop. On 12 May, President Rousseff was stripped of her powers and duties for 180 days, after an <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_process_against_Dilma_Rousseff" class="mw-redirect" title="Impeachment process against Dilma Rousseff">impeachment</a> vote in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Senate" title="Federal Senate">Federal Senate</a>, thus Vice President <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a> acted as acting president during the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 October 2017, the head of the Brazilian Olympic Committee <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Arthur_Nuzman" title="Carlos Arthur Nuzman">Carlos Nuzman</a>, was arrested amid an money laundering investigation that a $2 million payment was made to secure votes for the bid to bring the Olympics to Rio. The money was allegedly paid to <a href="/wiki/Lamine_Diack" title="Lamine Diack">Lamine Diack</a> and his son Papa Massata who was a member of the IOC at the time of the alleged payment which was three days before the vote in 2009. All 3 were charged with money laundering along with the former governor of Rio state <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Cabral" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergio Cabral">Sergio Cabral</a>, who was already in prison for money laundering offences at the time, Brazilian businessman Arthur Soares and ex Brazilian Olympic Committee chief Leonardo Gryner. All 6 were charged with running a criminal organisation, money laundering and violating currency laws in their own native countries.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On 4 July 2019 it was reported that Cabral told a judge the money went to Diack, the former president of the International Association of Athletics Federations (IAAF) and was used to buy as many as nine votes.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zika_virus">Zika virus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Zika virus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Zika_virus_epidemic" title="2015–16 Zika virus epidemic">2015–16 Zika virus epidemic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg/220px-Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg/330px-Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg/440px-Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1396" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dengue_Votuporanga.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Agent for endemic diseases of the city of <a href="/wiki/Votuporanga" title="Votuporanga">Votuporanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a></div></div></div>
<p>An <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Zika_virus_epidemic" title="2015–16 Zika virus epidemic">outbreak</a> of the mosquito-borne <a href="/wiki/Zika_virus" title="Zika virus">Zika virus</a> in Brazil raised fears regarding its potential impact on athletes and visitors. To prevent puddles of stagnant water that allow mosquitoes to breed, organisers announced plans to perform daily inspections of Olympic venues.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Zika virus transmission was also attributed to <a href="#Sanitation">inefficient sewage treatment</a> in the area—an issue that was also in the process of being addressed for the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantic_20160331_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atlantic_20160331-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2016, a group of 150 physicians and scientists sent an open letter to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, calling upon them to, according to co-author <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Caplan" title="Arthur Caplan">Arthur Caplan</a>, have "an open, transparent discussion of the risks of holding the Olympics as planned in Brazil". The WHO dismissed the request, stating that "cancelling or changing the location of the 2016 Olympics will not significantly alter the international spread of Zika virus", and that there was "no public health justification" for postponing them.<sup id="cite_ref-quartz-goahead_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quartz-goahead-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wp-150experts_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-150experts-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc-whono_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-whono-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/List_of_athletes_not_attending_Rio_Olympics_due_to_Zika_virus_concerns" title="List of athletes not attending Rio Olympics due to Zika virus concerns">Some athletes</a> did not attend the Games because of the epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On 2 September 2016, however, the World Health Organization reported that there were no confirmed cases of Zika among athletes or visitors during the Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-nozikaactually_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-nozikaactually-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_Brazil" title="Environmental issues in Brazil">Environmental issues in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Brazil" title="Water supply and sanitation in Brazil">Water supply and sanitation in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg/220px-Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg/330px-Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg/440px-Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Forte_de_Copacabana_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fort_Copacabana" title="Fort Copacabana">Fort Copacabana</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/Cycling_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Cycling at the 2016 Summer Olympics">cycling road race</a> (start and finish), <a href="/wiki/Marathon_swimming" title="Marathon swimming">marathon swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> events.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Guanabara_Bay" title="Guanabara Bay">Guanabara Bay</a>, whose waters were used for sailing and windsurfing competitions, is heavily polluted. Among the chief causes of the pollution are uncollected trash fed into the bay via polluted rivers and <a href="/wiki/Slum" title="Slum">slums</a> along the coast. Pollution of the Guanabara has been a long-term issue. Officials promised at the <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">Earth Summit</a> in 1992 that they would begin to address the pollution but previous attempts to do so have been insufficient. As an aspect of their bid for the Games, Rio once again committed to making efforts towards cleaning the bay.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-pollution_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-pollution-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> However, some of these proposed initiatives have faced budgetary issues.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-fundingclean_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-fundingclean-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Prior to these efforts, only 17% of Rio's sewage was treated;<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-germannfect_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-germannfect-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> this <a href="/wiki/Raw_sewage" class="mw-redirect" title="Raw sewage">raw sewage</a> also leaked into the bay. Although Mayor of Rio <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Paes" title="Eduardo Paes">Eduardo Paes</a> stated that the city may not be able to reach its goal of having 80% of sewage treated,<sup id="cite_ref-wp-superbug_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-superbug-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> at least 60% of sewage was treated by March 2016, with a projected goal of 65% of sewage being treated by the time the Olympics started.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Brazil" title="Crime in Brazil">Crime in Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Brazil" title="Terrorism in Brazil">Terrorism in Brazil</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_(FAB)_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg/220px-For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg/330px-For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg/440px-For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_%28FAB%29_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3573" data-file-height="2378" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:For%C3%A7a_A%C3%A9rea_Brasileira_(FAB)_faz_treinamento_de_intercepta%C3%A7%C3%A3o_a%C3%A9rea_para_os_Jogos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Northrop_F-5" title="Northrop F-5">F-5EM Tiger II</a> fighter jet of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">Brazilian Air Force</a> during an air intercept training for the Rio 2016.</div></div></div>
<p>Rio's crime problems also received renewed attention after it was awarded the Games; Mayor Paes stated that the city was facing "big issues" in heightening security, but that such concerns and issues were presented to the IOC throughout the bidding process.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The governor of the state of Rio de Janeiro also highlighted the fact that London faced security problems, with a <a href="/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">terrorist attack</a> occurring just one day after it was awarded the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. The estimate was that 5,000 men of the <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Security_Force" title="National Public Security Force">National Public Security Force</a> and 22,000 military officers (14,800 <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Army" title="Brazilian Army">Army</a>; 5,900 <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Navy" title="Brazilian Navy">Navy</a> and 1,300 of the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Air_Force" title="Brazilian Air Force">Brazilian Air Force</a>), in addition to the fixed quota of Rio January, would act during the Olympic Games.<sup id="cite_ref-terror_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terror-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 July 2016, two weeks before the scheduled start of the Games, the <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_Federal_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian Federal Police">Brazilian Federal Police</a> broke up an <a href="/wiki/Islamic_terrorism" title="Islamic terrorism">Islamic jihadist terrorist</a> ring by arresting 12 people.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_doping_scandal">Russian doping scandal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2016_Summer_Olympics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Russian doping scandal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_Russia" title="Doping in Russia">Doping in Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/McLaren_Report" title="McLaren Report">McLaren Report</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG/220px-%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG/330px-%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG/440px-%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9E%D0%9A%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Olympic_Committee" title="Russian Olympic Committee">Russian Olympic Committee</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a></div></div></div>
<p>Media attention began growing in December 2014 when German broadcaster <a href="/wiki/ARD_(broadcaster)" title="ARD (broadcaster)">ARD</a> reported on state-sponsored doping in Russia, comparing it to <a href="/wiki/Doping_in_East_Germany" title="Doping in East Germany">doping in East Germany</a>. In November 2015, the <a href="/wiki/World_Anti-Doping_Agency" title="World Anti-Doping Agency">World Anti-Doping Agency</a> (WADA) published a report and the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Athletics_Federations" title="International Association of Athletics Federations">International Association of Athletics Federations</a> (IAAF) suspended Russia indefinitely from world track and field events. The United Kingdom Anti-Doping agency later assisted WADA with testing in Russia. In June 2016, they reported that they were unable to fully carry out their work and noted intimidation by armed <a href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service" title="Federal Security Service">Federal Security Service</a> (FSB) agents.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> After a Russian former lab director made allegations about the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a>, WADA commissioned an independent investigation led by <a href="/wiki/Richard_McLaren_(academic)" title="Richard McLaren (academic)">Richard McLaren</a>. McLaren's investigation found corroborating evidence, concluding in a report published in July 2016 that the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Sport_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Sport (Russia)">Ministry of Sport</a> and the FSB had operated a "state-directed failsafe system" using a "disappearing positive [test] methodology" (DPM) from "at least late 2011 to August 2015".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to these findings, WADA announced that RUSADA should be regarded as non-compliant with respect to the World Anti-Doping Code and recommended that Russia be banned from competing at the 2016 Summer Olympics.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The IOC rejected the recommendation, stating that the IOC and each sport's <a href="/wiki/List_of_international_sports_federations" title="List of international sports federations">international federation</a> would make decisions on each athlete's individual basis.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> One day prior to the opening ceremony, 278 athletes were cleared to compete under the Russian flag, while 111 were removed because of doping.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In contrast, the entire Kuwaiti team was banned from competing under their own flag (for a non-doping related matter).<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Unlike the IOC, the <a href="/wiki/International_Paralympic_Committee" title="International Paralympic Committee">International Paralympic Committee</a> voted unanimously to ban the entire <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_2016_Summer_Paralympics" title="Russia at the 2016 Summer Paralympics">Russian team</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Paralympics" title="2016 Summer Paralympics">2016 Summer Paralympics</a> and suspended the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Paralympic_Committee" title="Russian Paralympic Committee">Russian Paralympic Committee</a>, having found evidence that the DPM was also in operation at the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Paralympics" title="2014 Winter Paralympics">2014 Winter Paralympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
